U.S. Treasury Secretary Tim Geithner says the Treasury Department plans to reopen the TARP program to funnel additional capital into smaller banks using funds it expects to receive from larger banks repaying their TARP loans.



AMEX, JPMORGAN TO SELL NON-FDIC CORPORATE BONDS

American Express and JPMorgan Chase are expected to sell $500 million each of corporate bonds not guaranteed by the FDIC. Move comes as several TARP recipients begin selling corporate bonds in an effort to try to shed government influence.



WHITE HOUSE REPORT NOTES PROGRESS ON STIMULUS PLAN


Page 200 of 226 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Obama administration says the $787 billion economic recovery package is beginning to show early signs of progress, while Republicans complain too many stimulus dollars are going into wasteful projects.



GOOGLE'S CHENG TO JOIN BLOOMBERG MULTIMEDIA

Ien Cheng, a product management director at Google, is named chief of staff at Bloomberg where he will oversee Bloomberg's television, radio, Web and mobile properties as company reduces reliance on financial-data "terminals" sales.



US AUTO OUTPUT EXPECTED TO FALL BY A THIRD

North American auto production this year is expected to fall by a third from 2008 to 8.4 million, according to a new industry forecast. IHS Global Insight cut another 150,000 vehicles from its late April estimate.

BB&T FILES APPLICATION TO REPAY TARP

BB&T says it filed its application to repay the $3.1 billion it had received from the U.S. Treasury's TARP. The bank established a capital plan with a $1.5 billion stock offering, $800 million in debt raised earlier, and $725 million in savings from cutting its dividend.



GEITHNER SEES PROGRESS IN MORTGAGE CRACKDOWN

U.S. Treasury Secretary Timothy Geithner says he's starting to see evidence that a new
multi-agency effort to combat a wave of mortgage-fraud and foreclosure-rescue scams is starting
to work.



FORMER FDIC CHAIRMAN SEIDMAN DIES AT 88

L. William Seidman, former chairman of the Federal Deposit Insurance Corp., dies at age 88 after a brief undisclosed illness, CNBC reports. Seidman recently had served as chief commentator at the network.

MGM MIRAGE EYES SENIOR SECURED BONDS

The casino company controlled by billionaire investor Kirk Kerkorian plans to raise $1.5 billion in the junk bond market as it takes advantage of increased risk appetite to pay down near-term debt maturities to avoid default.



GM SHARES BRIEFLY HIT LOW OF $1

After trading at more than $40 less than two years ago, shares of General Motors briefly touch $1 a share amid concerns it will file for Chapter 11 protection. The shares recently rebounded to
$1.22, up 6%.



HEDGE FUNDS WORRY ABOUT PPIP PARTICIPATION

Hedge fund managers worry that if months from now Public-Private Investment
Partnership-linked deals yield solid returns for fund managers, lawmakers may change rules,
paying a lower amount legislators deem fair.


INTEL TO APPEAL &EURO;1.06B FINE FOR EU ANTITRUST VIOLATION


Page 201 of 226 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Intel says it is going to appeal the European Commission's decision to  fine the company a record EUR1.06 billion for breaking European antitrust laws. Intel is said to have provided rebates to computer makers if they bought most of their computer chips from  Intel.



OBAMA SUPREME COURT PICK EXPECTED SOON

Senate Majority Leader Harry Reid, D-Nev., and Senate Judiciary Committee Chair Patrick Leahy, D-Vt., emerge from a meeting with President Obama saying they are confident a new justice will be on the bench in October.



US BANCORP: MORTGAGE APPLICATIONS STEADY

U.S. Bancorp's Chairman and Chief Executive Richard Davis says that the volume of mortgage applications this quarter remains strong, but that loan growth overall remains hampered by subdued demand from borrowers.



FORD SELLS 300M COMMON SHARES AT  $4.75

The only U.S. automaker not taking government aid sells $1.4 billion in stock, raising money it will use for a variety of corporate purposes and to fund a retiree health program. The
$4.75-a-share price is a 5.2% discount to the stock's closing price of $5.01 Tuesday. Shares fall
4%.



CITIGROUP FILES TO ADD 1.6B SHARES TO OFFER

Citigroup files with the SEC to register about 1.6 billion more common shares as part of its move to convert preferred stock to common shares. Move is in addition to its March filing to register about 4.38 billion common shares under its exchange offer. Shares fall 4%.



RR DONNELLEY PROPOSES QUEBECOR BUYOUT

R.R. Donnelley announces that it has written to rival printer Quebecor World to say it is interested in buying the company for $1.35 billion, saying its can offer creditors and better terms than a proposed reorganization plan. R.R. Donnelley's shares fall 6%.



OIL CLOSES DOWN $1.39 A BARREL AT $57.46

Oil futures close lower after government data showed U.S. crude inventories shrank for the first time since February.



US LAWMAKERS QUESTION SECRECY AT AIG

The U.S. government's rescue of AIG and the long-term plans to pay back taxpayer funds remain shrouded in secrecy, U.S. lawmakers assert, chiding the firm for not being forthcoming with answers.



DR PEPPER SNAPPLE NET UP 39%; UPS EPS FORECAST

Company's 1Q earnings rise to $132 million, or 52c on a gain related to changes in distribution agreements. Beverage giant boosts its full-year EPS forecast to a range of $1.70 to $1.78 a share. Revenue decreases 2% to $1.26 billion. Shares up 3%.

Page 202 of 226 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
MACY'S, LIZ CLAIBORNE POST WIDER LOSSES

Macy's loss widens to $88 million, or 21c a share, while Liz Claiborne posts a net loss of $91 million, illustrating that the recession hasn't ended for many mid-tier sellers and makers of apparel. Macy's shares fall 5%; Liz slides 23%.

It seems inconceivable that an Italian company, Fiat, is dotting the i's and crossing the t's in the documents that will give it control of Chrysler. We all remember when Daimler-Benz of Stuttgart, Germany, bought Chrysler.

An unexpected dip in retail sales in April sends the Dow Jones Industrial Average down more than 150 points and hurt the price of oil and other economically sensitive investments.

TD



US APRIL RETAIL SALES SLIP 0.4%

U.S. retail sales fall for a second consecutive month in April, beaten below expectations by a recession that's cost nearly 6 million jobs. Retail sales slip by 0.4% compared to the prior month. Economists expected a 0.1% increase.



US LAWMAKERS QUESTION SECRECY AT AIG

The U.S. government's rescue of AIG and the long-term plans to pay back taxpayer funds remain shrouded in secrecy, U.S. lawmakers assert, chiding the firm for not being forthcoming with answers.

U.S. Treasury Secretary Timothy Geithner says he's starting to see evidence that a new multi-agency effort to combat a wave of mortgage-fraud and foreclosure-rescue scams is starting to work.

U.S. senators push several amendments to credit-card legislation that would make it even more unfriendly to banks, in a sign of how unpopular the industry has become on Capitol Hill.

AK STEEL TO IDLE KENTUCKY OPERATIONS

AK Steel will likely turn off its blast furnaces, idling 750 workers in Ashland, Ky., in midsummer, possibly to the end of the year, as flat-rolled steel demand plummets with GM and Chrysler shutting down production. Shares drop 12%.

DOW JONES NEWSWIRES

European Union  Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes is seeking to fineIntel  Corp. (INTC) more than EUR1 billion ($1.36 billion) for breaking European  antitrust rules, Bloomberg News reported on its Web site Tuesday, citing a person with direct knowledge of the case.

TD
The fine, which would be a record, could be reduced, Bloomberg reported the person as saying. The  fine
could be changed because of its size and the nature of rebate-related  antitrust cases, it said.
The European Commission is due to make the ruling known Wednesday, Bloomberg said.

HD      DJ Intel Faces EUR1.06B Antitrust Fine For Blocking Competition
WC     366 words
PD      13 May 2009
ET       02:47 PM
SN      Dow Jones Chinese Financial Wire
SC      DJCFWE
LA       English
CY      Copyright (c) 2009, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--Intel Corp. (INTC) will have to pay a record  fine of EUR1.06 billion for breaking European antitrust laws, the  European Commission said Wednesday.

The executive arm of the European Union, found the world's largest computer chip maker illegally kept its smaller rival Advanced Micro Devices Inc. (AMD), of Sunnyvale, Calif. out of  competition by paying computer manufacturers and retailers not to use AMD's products.

TD
The commission found  Intel provided rebates to computer makers on condition they bought most - often up to 95% - of their computer chips from  Intel. Intel also made direct payments to major retail chain MediaMarkt so it would only sell computers with Intel's chips, the commission said.

Intel also paid computer manufacturers to halt or delay the launch of the residual number of computers which contained AMD's chips in order to even further reduce customer choice, the commission said.
The commission has ordered  Intel to stop these practices immediately, and said it would actively monitor
Intel's compliance with its decision.

The computer manufacturers which  Intel used to give payments to are: Acer (2353.TW), Dell (DELL), Hewlet Packard (HPQ), Lenovo (0992.HK) and NEC Corp.(6701.TO).

'Intel has harmed millions of European consumers by deliberately acting to keep competitors out of the market for computer chips for many years. Such a serious and sustained violation of the E.U.'s  antitrust rules cannot be tolerated,' said  Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes.

The commission estimates the world market in the specific chip set in question, namely the x86 CPUs, to be worth about EUR22 billion (or $30 billion) a year, with Europe accounting for approximately 30% of that.
-By Peppi Kiviniemi, Dow Jones Newswires; +32 (0)2 741 1483; peppi.kiviniemi@dowjones.com

DOW JONES NEWSWIRES

European Union  Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes is seeking to fineIntel  Corp. (INTC) more than EUR1 billion ($1.36 billion) for breaking European  antitrust rules, Bloomberg News reported on its Web site Tuesday, citing a person with direct knowledge of the case.

TD
The fine, which would be a record, could be reduced, Bloomberg reported the person as saying. The
fine could be changed because of its size and the nature of rebate-related  antitrust cases, it said.
The European Commission is due to make the ruling known Wednesday, Bloomberg said.

HD            News Highlights: Top Equities  Stories Of The Day
WC           433 words
PD            13 May 2009

SN            Dow Jones International News

LP



ALLIANZ 1Q NET PROFIT FALLS SHARPLY
Allianz, Europe's largest primary insurer by market capitalization, reports a substantial decline in 1Q net profit, on crisis-triggered write-downs on financial investments, a charge related to the sale of Dresdner Bank and higher claims costs.

TD



TELEFONICA NET UP 9.8%, REITERATES TARGETS
Telefonica says 1Q net profit rose 9.8% to EUR1.69 billion on resilience in Latin America. The figure, however, missed analysts' expectations. The company also reiterates its 2009 outlook.



EUROPEAN STOCKS TRADE CAUTIOUSLY
Europe's major stock indexes lack direction, as the broader macroeconomic picture keeps investors cautious and sends some back to risk-aversion strategies.



EU
FINES INTEL EUR1.06B FOR ANTITRUST VIOLATION
Intel will have to pay a record fine of EUR1.06 billion for breaking European  antitrust laws, the European Commission says. Intel provided rebates to computer makers if they bought most of their computer chips from Intel.



SAINSBURY PROFIT UP 11%, EXPECTS FURTHER GROWTH
U.K. grocer J Sainsbury continues its resurgence by posting an 11% rise in annual profit, boosted by sales of its own-label products, and says it will continue its good progress by offering customers strong service and good deals.



US OFFICIALS REPORTEDLY KNEW OF AIG BONUSES
U.S. federal officials were aware of controversial bonuses paid by taxpayer-bailed out insurance giant AIG months before they sparked a firestorm, a press reports says. --WSJ: AIG Trustees Seeking New Board, CEO



L&G, AMLIN POST STRONG 1Q SALES; OUTLOOK IMPROVING
U.K. insurers Legal & General and Amlin post strong 1Q sales and indicate that there are signs of improvement in financial markets in general. The positive results and some upbeat comments come amid the continuing rise in U.K. insurance stocks.

Page 222 of 226 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
LAGARDERE REVENUE BEATS VIEWS, CONFIRMS GUIDANCE
French media conglomerate Lagardere reports a slightly less-than-expected 2% decline in 1Q
revenue as its Lagardere Active division took a hit from the slumping advertising market.

UNICREDIT 1Q NET DOWN ON LOWER FEES
UniCredit says that 1Q net profit fell because of a decline in commission that was partially offset by better-than-expected net interest income and operating income.



DAIMLER TO CUT 2,300 JOBS AT JAPANESE UNIT
Daimler will cut 2,300 jobs at its Japanese truck unit by end of 2010 and cut the product portfolio by
50% due to a shrinking domestic market. The restructuring is expected to lead to earnings
improvement of EUR760 million by 2011. --Daimler Expects 2009 Loss At Japan Unit

HD         EUROPEAN MIDDAY BRIEFING FROM DOW JONES NEWSWIRES WC         1,131 words

AMERICAN MARKETS OUTLOOK: Stock futures indicate a flat to slightly lower start Wednesday, with investors expecting another busy session amid a raft of economic data.

"The major focus will be the retail sales numbers," said Ian Griffiths, dealer at spreadbettor CMC Markets. With Wal Mart results due Thursday, retailers will be in focus over the next couple of days, he said.

TD
Mortgage applications, import prices and oil inventory data are also due for release Wednesday.

"Investors will be looking for the Dow to push back through 8,500 and continue to rally up towards the highs of the year but after such a strong run it seems that the markets are running low on fuel," Griffiths said. "Opinion is beginning to change about the near-term future of global equity markets with many believing we have now hit the top of the rally," he said.

At 1035 GMT, S&P 500 futures were down 2.7 points at 904.1, Nasdaq 100 futures were down 9 points at 1376 and Dow industrial futures were down 21 points at 8415.

EUROPEAN MARKETS: European markets are lower around midday. Cyclical stocks, such as financials, weigh on the indexes, with ING Groep down 6.7%, Fortis 4.9% lower and BNP Paribas down
4.3%.
London's FTSE 100 is down 0.6% at 4399.04, as the market assesses the Bank of England's Inflation
Report. Rob Carnell, economist at ING Bank said the BOE's prediction of a return to modest growth in
2010 and above-trend growth in 2011-2012 is a little optimistic.
In Frankfurt, the DAX is down 0.8% at 4815.9, while in Paris, the CAC 40 is down 0.3% at 3220.3. Bunds and gilts are higher as European equities retreat. At 1029 GMT, June bunds were up 0.21 at
120.83 and June gilts were up 0.70 at 119.78.
Credit rating worries have hit the dollar, leaving it lower against most other majors in Europe. At 1029
GMT, the dollar was down at Y96.15, the euro was up at $1.3650, and the pound was down at
$1.5180.

BOE INFLATION REPORT KNOCKS STERLING: BOE Governor Mervyn King's downbeat and highly uncertain assessment of the U.K.'s economic outlook, including weaker growth forecasts, has wiped out sterling's gains against the euro.
